<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of scientists who disagree with the scientific consensus on global warming</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks">This is a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">dynamic list</a> and may never be able to satisfy particular standards for completeness. You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_scientists_who_disagree_with_the_scientific_consensus_on_global_warming&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a> with <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliably sourced</a> entries.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg/300px-Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg.png" width="300" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg/450px-Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg/600px-Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="357" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_science_opinion_graph_3Path.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nearly all publishing climate scientists (97–98%<sup id="cite_ref-Anderegg_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderegg-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>) are convinced by the evidence that humans are significantly contributing to global warming.<sup id="cite_ref-Anderegg_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderegg-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DZ_EOS_2009_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DZ_EOS_2009-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>This is a list of scientists who have made statements that conflict with the scientific consensus on <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> as summarized by the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a> and endorsed by other scientific bodies. A minority are climatologists. Nearly all publishing climate scientists (97–98%<sup id="cite_ref-Anderegg_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anderegg-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>) support the consensus on anthropogenic climate change,<sup id="cite_ref-doran_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doran-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> hence this list represents a minority viewpoint.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Scientific_consensus" title="Scientific consensus">scientific consensus</a> is that the global average surface temperature has risen over the last century. <a href="/wiki/Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change" title="Scientific opinion on climate change">Scientific opinion on climate change</a> was summarized in the 2001 <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Third_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Third Assessment Report">Third Assessment Report</a> of the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC). The main conclusions on global warming at that time were as follows:
</p>
<ol><li>The global <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_temperature_record" title="Instrumental temperature record">average surface temperature</a> has risen 0.6 ± 0.2&#160;°<a href="/wiki/Celsius" title="Celsius">C</a> since the late 19th century, and 0.17&#160;°C per decade in the years 1971–2001.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>"There is new and stronger evidence that most of the warming observed over the last 50 years is <a href="/wiki/Attribution_of_recent_climate_change" title="Attribution of recent climate change">attributable to human activities</a>", in particular emissions of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> carbon dioxide and methane.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>If greenhouse gas emissions continue the warming will also continue, with temperatures projected to increase by 1.4&#160;°C to 5.8&#160;°C between 1990 and 2100.<sup id="ref_A_1" class="reference"><a href="#cnote_A">[A]</a></sup> Accompanying this temperature increase will be increases in some types of extreme weather and a projected <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The balance of impacts of global warming become significantly negative at larger values of warming.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>These findings are recognized by the national science academies of all the major industrialized nations;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> the consensus has strengthened over time<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and is now virtually unanimous.<sup id="cite_ref-Powell-Unanimous_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powell-Unanimous-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>  The level of consensus correlates with expertise in climate science.<sup id="cite_ref-ConsensusOnConsensus_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConsensusOnConsensus-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There have been several efforts to compile lists of dissenting scientists, including a 2008 US senate minority report,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Petition" title="Oregon Petition">Oregon Petition</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and a 2007 list by the <a href="/wiki/Heartland_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Heartland Institute">Heartland Institute</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> all three of which have been criticized on a number of grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the purpose of this list, a "scientist" is defined as an individual who has published at least one peer-reviewed research article in the broad field of natural sciences, although not necessarily in a field relevant to climatology. Since the publication of the IPCC Third Assessment Report, each has made a clear statement in his or her own words (as opposed to the name being found on a petition, etc.) disagreeing with one or more of the report's three main conclusions, and each has been described in reliable sources as a climate skeptic, denier, or in disagreement with any of the three main conclusions. Their views on climate change are usually described in more detail in their biographical articles.  Few of the statements in the references for this list are part of the <a href="/wiki/Peer-reviewed" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-reviewed">peer-reviewed</a> scientific literature; most are from other sources such as interviews, opinion pieces, online essays and presentations.
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Nota_bene" title="Nota bene">Nota bene</a></i>: Only individuals who have their own Wikipedia article may be included in the list.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientists_questioning_the_accuracy_of_IPCC_climate_projections">Scientists questioning the accuracy of IPCC climate projections</span></h2>
<p>These scientists have said that it is not possible to project global climate accurately enough to justify the ranges projected for temperature and sea-level rise over the 21st century. They may not conclude specifically that the current IPCC projections are either too high or too low, but that the projections are likely to be inaccurate due to inadequacies of current global climate modeling.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/David_Bellamy" title="David Bellamy">David Bellamy</a>, botanist.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lennart_Bengtsson" title="Lennart Bengtsson">Lennart Bengtsson</a>, meteorologist, <a href="/wiki/Reading_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Reading University">Reading University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Piers_Corbyn" title="Piers Corbyn">Piers Corbyn</a>, owner of the business WeatherAction which makes weather forecasts.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Susan_Crockford" class="mw-redirect" title="Susan Crockford">Susan Crockford</a>, Zoologist, adjunct professor in Anthropology at the University of Victoria. <sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Judith_Curry" title="Judith Curry">Judith Curry</a>, professor and former chair of the School of Earth and Atmospheric Sciences at the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Institute_of_Technology" title="Georgia Institute of Technology">Georgia Institute of Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Uncertainty_Monster_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Uncertainty_Monster-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wicked_Problem_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wicked_Problem-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_D%27Aleo" title="Joseph D&#39;Aleo">Joseph D'Aleo</a>, past Chairman American Meteorological Society's Committee on Weather Analysis and Forecasting, former Professor of Meteorology, Lyndon State College.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Freeman_Dyson" title="Freeman Dyson">Freeman Dyson</a>, professor emeritus of the School of Natural Sciences, <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Advanced_Study" title="Institute for Advanced Study">Institute for Advanced Study</a>; <a href="/wiki/Fellow_of_the_Royal_Society" title="Fellow of the Royal Society">Fellow of the Royal Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cat_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cat-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ivar_Giaever" title="Ivar Giaever">Ivar Giaever</a>, Norwegian–American physicist and Nobel laureate in physics (1973).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Steven_E._Koonin" title="Steven E. Koonin">Steven E. Koonin</a>, theoretical physicist and director of the Center for Urban Science and Progress at New York University.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Lindzen" title="Richard Lindzen">Richard Lindzen</a>, Alfred P. Sloan emeritus professor of atmospheric science at the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cat_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cat-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ed.2008_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ed.2008-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientists_arguing_that_global_warming_is_primarily_caused_by_natural_processes">Scientists arguing that global warming is primarily caused by natural processes</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_Change_Attribution.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Climate_Change_Attribution.png/220px-Climate_Change_Attribution.png" width="220" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Climate_Change_Attribution.png/330px-Climate_Change_Attribution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Climate_Change_Attribution.png/440px-Climate_Change_Attribution.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Climate_Change_Attribution.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graph showing the ability with which a <a href="/wiki/Global_climate_model" class="mw-redirect" title="Global climate model">global climate model</a> is able to reconstruct the <a href="/wiki/Historical_temperature_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical temperature record">historical temperature record</a>, and the degree to which those temperature changes can be decomposed into various forcing factors. It shows the effects of five forcing factors: <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenhouse gases">greenhouse gases</a>, man-made <a href="/wiki/Sulfate" title="Sulfate">sulfate</a> emissions, <a href="/wiki/Solar_variation" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar variation">solar variability</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a> changes, and <a href="/wiki/Volcanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic">volcanic</a> emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>These scientists have said that the observed warming is more likely to be attributable to natural causes than to human activities. Their views on climate change are usually described in more detail in their biographical articles.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Khabibullo_Abdusamatov" class="mw-redirect" title="Khabibullo Abdusamatov">Khabibullo Abdusamatov</a>, astrophysicist at <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Observatory" title="Pulkovo Observatory">Pulkovo Observatory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Ian_Clark_(geologist)" title="Ian Clark (geologist)">Ian Clark</a>, hydrogeologist, professor, Department of Earth Sciences, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Ottawa" title="University of Ottawa">University of Ottawa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientists_arguing_that_the_cause_of_global_warming_is_unknown">Scientists arguing that the cause of global warming is unknown</span></h2>
<p>These scientists have said that no principal cause can be ascribed to the observed rising temperatures, whether man-made or natural.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Syun-Ichi_Akasofu" title="Syun-Ichi Akasofu">Syun-Ichi Akasofu</a>, retired professor of geophysics and founding director of the International Arctic Research Center of the University of Alaska Fairbanks.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claude_All%C3%A8gre" title="Claude Allègre">Claude Allègre</a>, French politician; geochemist, emeritus professor at Institute of Geophysics (Paris).<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Balling" title="Robert Balling">Robert Balling</a>, a professor of geography at <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/P%C3%A5l_Brekke" title="Pål Brekke">Pål Brekke</a>, solar astrophycisist, senior advisor <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Space_Centre" title="Norwegian Space Centre">Norwegian Space Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Christy" title="John Christy">John Christy</a>, professor of atmospheric science and director of the Earth System Science Center at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alabama_in_Huntsville" title="University of Alabama in Huntsville">University of Alabama in Huntsville</a>, contributor to several <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a> reports.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Petr_Chylek" class="mw-redirect" title="Petr Chylek">Petr Chylek</a>, space and remote sensing sciences researcher, <a href="/wiki/Los_Alamos_National_Laboratory" title="Los Alamos National Laboratory">Los Alamos National Laboratory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Deming" title="David Deming">David Deming</a>, geology professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oklahoma" title="University of Oklahoma">University of Oklahoma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stanley_B._Goldenberg" title="Stanley B. Goldenberg">Stanley B. Goldenberg</a> a meteorologist with NOAA/AOML's Hurricane Research Division.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vincent_R._Gray" title="Vincent R. Gray">Vincent R. Gray</a>, New Zealand physical chemist with expertise in coal ashes.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Keith_E._Idso" title="Keith E. Idso">Keith E. Idso</a>, botanist, former adjunct professor of biology at <a href="/wiki/Maricopa_County_Community_College_District" title="Maricopa County Community College District">Maricopa County Community College District</a> and the vice president of the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_the_Study_of_Carbon_Dioxide_and_Global_Change" title="Center for the Study of Carbon Dioxide and Global Change">Center for the Study of Carbon Dioxide and Global Change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kary_Mullis" title="Kary Mullis">Kary Mullis</a>, 1993 Nobel laureate in chemistry, inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Polymerase_chain_reaction" title="Polymerase chain reaction">polymerase chain reaction</a> (PCR) method.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antonino_Zichichi" title="Antonino Zichichi">Antonino Zichichi</a>, emeritus professor of nuclear physics at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a> and president of the <a href="/wiki/World_Federation_of_Scientists" title="World Federation of Scientists">World Federation of Scientists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientists_arguing_that_global_warming_will_have_few_negative_consequences">Scientists arguing that global warming will have few negative consequences</span></h2>
<p>These scientists have said that projected rising temperatures will be of little impact or a net positive for society or the environment.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Indur_M._Goklany" title="Indur M. Goklany">Indur M. Goklany</a>, electrical engineer, science and technology policy analyst for the United States <a href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Interior" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of the Interior">Department of the Interior</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Craig_D._Idso" title="Craig D. Idso">Craig D. Idso</a>, geographer, faculty researcher, Office of Climatology, <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a> and founder of the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_the_Study_of_Carbon_Dioxide_and_Global_Change" title="Center for the Study of Carbon Dioxide and Global Change">Center for the Study of Carbon Dioxide and Global Change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-C_Idso_quot_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C_Idso_quot-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sherwood_B._Idso" title="Sherwood B. Idso">Sherwood B. Idso</a>, former research physicist, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">USDA</a> Water Conservation Laboratory, and adjunct professor, <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Idso_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Idso-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Michaels" title="Patrick Michaels">Patrick Michaels</a>, senior fellow at the <a href="/wiki/Cato_Institute" title="Cato Institute">Cato Institute</a> and retired <a href="/wiki/Research_professor" class="mw-redirect" title="Research professor">research professor</a> of environmental science at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Virginia" title="University of Virginia">University of Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Deceased_scientists">Deceased scientists</span></h2>
<p>These scientists published material indicating their opposition to the mainstream scientific assessment of global warming prior to their deaths.   	
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/August_H._Auer_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="August H. Auer Jr.">August H. "Augie" Auer Jr.</a> (1940–2007), retired <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_Service_of_New_Zealand_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Meteorological Service of New Zealand Limited">New Zealand MetService</a> meteorologist and past professor of atmospheric science at the University of Wyoming.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Reid_Bryson" title="Reid Bryson">Reid Bryson</a> (1920–2008), <a href="/wiki/Emeritus#In_academia" title="Emeritus">emeritus professor</a> of atmospheric and oceanic sciences, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin-Madison" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Wisconsin-Madison">University of Wisconsin-Madison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_M._Carter" title="Robert M. Carter">Robert M. Carter</a> (1942–2016), former head of the School of Earth Sciences at <a href="/wiki/James_Cook_University" title="James Cook University">James Cook University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chris_de_Freitas" title="Chris de Freitas">Chris de Freitas</a> (1948–2017), associate professor, School of Geography, Geology and Environmental Science, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Auckland" title="University of Auckland">University of Auckland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_M._Gray" title="William M. Gray">William M. Gray</a> (1929–2016), professor emeritus and head of the <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Meteorology_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Meteorology Project">Tropical Meteorology Project</a>, Department of Atmospheric Science, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yuri_Izrael" title="Yuri Izrael">Yuri Izrael</a> (1930–2014), former chairman, Committee for Hydrometeorology (USSR); former firector, Institute of Global Climate and Ecology (Russian Academy of Science); vice-chairman of <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">IPCC</a>, 2001-2007.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Jastrow" title="Robert Jastrow">Robert Jastrow</a> (1925–2008), American <a href="/wiki/Astronomer" title="Astronomer">astronomer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">physicist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">cosmologist</a> and leading <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> scientist who, together with <a href="/wiki/Fred_Seitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Fred Seitz">Fred Seitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Nierenberg" title="William Nierenberg">William Nierenberg</a>, established the <a href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall_Institute" title="George C. Marshall Institute">George C. Marshall Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-marshall2_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marshall2-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harold_Lewis" title="Harold Lewis">Harold ("Hal") Warren Lewis</a> (1923–2011), <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emeritus</a> professor of <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> and former department chairman at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara" title="University of California, Santa Barbara">University of California, Santa Barbara</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LewisLtr_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LewisLtr-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Seitz" title="Frederick Seitz">Frederick Seitz</a> (1911–2008), <a href="/wiki/Solid-state_physics" title="Solid-state physics">solid-state physicist</a>, former president of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a> and co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/George_C._Marshall_Institute" title="George C. Marshall Institute">George C. Marshall Institute</a> in 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-marshall1_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marshall1-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seitz_quote_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seitz_quote-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div style=""><ol class="references" style="list-style-type:upper-alpha;">
<li id="cnote_A"><b><a href="#ref_A_1">^</a></b> In its 2007 assessment report, IPCC projected likely temperature rise for various hypothetical levels of future greenhouse gas emissions, known as <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">"emissions scenarios"</a>. They reported that during the 21st century the global surface temperature is likely to rise a further 1.1 to 2.9&#160;°C (2.0 to 5.2&#160;°F) for the lowest emissions scenario used in the report, and 2.4 to 6.4&#160;°C (4.3 to 11.5&#160;°F) for the highest.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li id="cnote_B"><b><a href="#ref_B_1">^</a></b> The compilation criteria for including scientists in the list is that they are relevant enough to have their own Wikipedia article, according to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Notability" title="Wikipedia:Notability">Wikipedia's notability guidelines</a>.</li>
</ol></div>

<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Koonin, Steven (September 2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://online.wsj.com/articles/climate-science-is-not-settled-1411143565">"Climate Science Is Not Settled"</a>. Enligt de vetenskapliga principer som växt fram under hundratals år tyder de senaste 20 årens observationer snarare på att hypotesen är falsk. (Own translation to English: The IPCC does not make its own research, but is a group searching for a given hypothesis – that carbon dioxide is crucial for the earth’s future climate. This is actually impossible since nobody has yet clarifed the climate system’s natural variability. According to the scientific principles that have developed over hundreds of years, the last 20 years of observations rather indicate that the hypothesis is false.)</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Expressen%2C+g%C3%A5+inte+p%C3%A5+klimatbluffen&amp;rft.date=2014-01-12&amp;rft.au=Peter+Stilbs&amp;rft.au=%C3%85ke+Ortmark&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.expressen.se%2Fdebatt%2Fexpressen-ga-inte-pa-klimatbluffen%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-135"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-135">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Svensmark, Henrik (2007). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.space.dtu.dk/upload/institutter/space/forskning/05_afdelinger/sun-climate/full_text_publications/svensmark_2007cosmoclimatology.pdf">"Cosmoclimatology: a new theory emerges"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Astronomy &amp; Geophysics</i>. <b>48</b> (1): 18–24<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">December 19,</span> 2011</span>. <q>The case for anthropogenic climate change during the 20th century rests primarily on the fact that concentrations of carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases increased and so did global temperatures. Attempts to show that certain details in the climatic record confirm the greenhouse forcing (e.g. Mitchell et al. 2001) have been less than conclusive. By contrast, the hypothesis that changes in cloudiness obedient to cosmic rays help to force climate change predicts a distinctive signal that is in fact very easily observed, as an exception that proves the rule.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Astronomy+%26+Geophysics&amp;rft.atitle=Cosmoclimatology%3A+a+new+theory+emerges&amp;rft.volume=48&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=18-24&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.au=Svensmark%2C+Henrik&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.space.dtu.dk%2Fupload%2Finstitutter%2Fspace%2Fforskning%2F05_afdelinger%2Fsun-climate%2Ffull_text_publications%2Fsvensmark_2007cosmoclimatology.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Veizer, Ján (2005). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://journals.hil.unb.ca/index.php/GC/article/view/2691">"Celestial Climate Driver: A Perspective from Four Billion Years of the Carbon Cycle"</a>. <i>Geoscience Canada</i>. 1. <b>32</b><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">26 August</span> 2012</span>. <q>At this stage, two scenarios of potential human impact on climate appear feasible: (1) the standard IPCC model that advocates the leading role of greenhouse gases, particularly of CO<sub>2</sub>, and (2) the alternative model that argues for celestial phenomena as the principal climate driver. The two scenarios are likely not even mutually exclusive, but a prioritization may result in different relative impact. Models and empirical observations are both indispensable tools of science, yet when discrepancies arise, observations should carry greater weight than theory. If so, the multitude of empirical observations favours celestial phenomena as the most important driver of terrestrial climate on most time scales, but time will be the final judge.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Geoscience+Canada&amp;rft.atitle=Celestial+Climate+Driver%3A+A+Perspective+from+Four+Billion+Years+of+the+Carbon+Cycle&amp;rft.volume=32&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.aulast=Veizer&amp;rft.aufirst=J%C3%A1n&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fjournals.hil.unb.ca%2Findex.php%2FGC%2Farticle%2Fview%2F2691&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-141"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-141">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Syun-Ichi, Akasofu (June 15, 2007). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://pielkeclimatesci.wordpress.com/2007/06/15/on-the-fundamental-defect-in-the-ipcc%E2%80%99s-approach-to-global-warming-research-by-syun-ichi-akasofu/">"On the Fundamental Defect in the IPCC's Approach to Global Warming Research by Syun-Ichi Akasofu"</a>. <i>Climate Science: Roger Pielke Sr</i>. <a href="/wiki/Wordpress.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Wordpress.com">wordpress.com</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">31 August</span> 2012</span>. <q>[T]he method of study adopted by the International Panel of Climate Change (IPCC) is fundamentally flawed, resulting in a baseless conclusion: <i>Most of the observed increase in globally averaged temperatures since the mid-20th century is very likely due to the observed increase in anthropogenic greenhouse gas concentrations.</i> Contrary to this statement ..., there is so far no definitive evidence that 'most' of the present warming is due to the greenhouse effect. ... [The IPCC] should have recognized that the range of observed natural changes should not be ignored, and thus their conclusion should be very tentative. The term 'most' in their conclusion is baseless.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Climate+Science%3A+Roger+Pielke+Sr.&amp;rft.atitle=On+the+Fundamental+Defect+in+the+IPCC%E2%80%99s+Approach+to+Global+Warming+Research+by+Syun-Ichi+Akasofu&amp;rft.date=2007-06-15&amp;rft.aulast=Syun-Ichi&amp;rft.aufirst=Akasofu&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fpielkeclimatesci.wordpress.com%2F2007%2F06%2F15%2Fon-the-fundamental-defect-in-the-ipcc%25E2%2580%2599s-approach-to-global-warming-research-by-syun-ichi-akasofu%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20061117230538/http://www.lexpress.fr/idees/tribunes/dossier/allegre/dossier.asp?ida=452950">"Climat: la prévention, oui, la peur, non"</a> (in French). <a href="/wiki/L%27Express_(France)" class="mw-redirect" title="L&#39;Express (France)">L'Express</a>. May 10, 2006. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lexpress.fr/idees/tribunes/dossier/allegre/dossier.asp?ida=452950">the original</a> on November 17, 2006<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 26,</span> 2011</span>. <q>:The increase in the CO<sub>2</sub> content of the atmosphere is an observed fact and mankind is most certainly responsible. In the long term, this increase will without doubt become harmful, but its exact role in the climate is less clear. Various parameters appear more important than CO<sub>2</sub>. Consider the water cycle and formation of various types of clouds, and the complex effects of industrial or agricultural dust. Or fluctuations of the intensity of the solar radiation on annual and century scale, which seem better correlated with heating effects than the variations of CO<sub>2</sub> content.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Climat%3A+la+pr%C3%A9vention%2C+oui%2C+la+peur%2C+non&amp;rft.date=2006-05-10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.lexpress.fr%2Fidees%2Ftribunes%2Fdossier%2Fallegre%2Fdossier.asp%3Fida%3D452950&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-145"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-145">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Balling, Robert (September 2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060222090652/http://www.marshall.org/pdf/materials/170.pdf">"The Increase in Global Temperature: What it Does and Does Not Tell Us"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. George C. Marshall Institute. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.marshall.org/pdf/materials/170.pdf">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on February 22, 2006. <q>[I]t is very likely that the recent upward trend [in global surface temperature] is very real and that the upward signal is greater than any noise introduced from uncertainties in the record. However, the general error is most likely to be in the warming direction, with a maximum possible (though unlikely) value of 0.3&#160;°C. ... At this moment in time we know only that: (1) Global surface temperatures have risen in recent decades. (2) Mid-tropospheric temperatures have warmed little over the same period. (3) This difference is not consistent with predictions from numerical climate models.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=The+Increase+in+Global+Temperature%3A+What+it+Does+and+Does+Not+Tell+Us&amp;rft.date=2003-09&amp;rft.aulast=Balling&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.marshall.org%2Fpdf%2Fmaterials%2F170.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-147"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-147">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Jacobsen, Siw Ellen (February 29, 2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.forskningsradet.no/en/Newsarticle/Pl_Brekke_Internationally_renowned_climate_sceptic_and_solar_expert/1236685401212?lang=en">"Pål Brekke: Internationally renowned climate sceptic and solar expert"</a>. The Research Council of Norway. <q>The UN Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPPC) has determined that the earth's temperature has risen by about 0.7° C since 1901. According to Dr Brekke, this time period coincides not only with an increase in human-caused greenhouse gas emissions, but also with a higher level of solar activity, which makes it complicated to separate the effects of these two phenomena. [...]  Dr Brekke has published more than 40 scientific articles on the sun and on the interaction between the sun and the earth. "We could be in for a surprise," he cautions. "It's possible that the sun plays an even more central role in global warming than we have suspected. Anyone who claims that the debate is over and the conclusions are firm has a fundamentally unscientific approach to one of the most momentous issues of our time."</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=P%C3%A5l+Brekke%3A+Internationally+renowned+climate+sceptic+and+solar+expert&amp;rft.date=2008-02-29&amp;rft.au=Jacobsen%2C+Siw+Ellen&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.forskningsradet.no%2Fen%2FNewsarticle%2FPl_Brekke_Internationally_renowned_climate_sceptic_and_solar_expert%2F1236685401212%3Flang%3Den&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+scientists+who+disagree+with+the+scientific+consensus+on+global+warming" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
